  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_312cf2a7-4860-452d-8f7c-089f068c1d9d'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer7334371207643240117">When her best guy friend falls victim to a vicious hate crime, sixteen-year-old Cat sets out to discover who in her small town did it.   <span id="freeText7334371207643240117" style="display:none">When her best guy friend falls victim to a vicious hate crime, sixteen-year-old Cat sets out to discover who in her small town did it. Richly atmospheric, this daring mystery mines the secrets of a tightly knit Southern community and examines the strength of will it takes to go against everyone you know in the name of justice.<br /><br />Against a backdrop of poverty, clannishness, drugs, and intolerance, Myracle has crafted a harrowing coming-of-age tale couched in a deeply intelligent mystery. Smart, fearless, and compassionate, this is an unforgettable work from a beloved author.</span>

This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    This is the only way you can learn how to read a book:<br />First, you must slay 5 dragons with a sword made from steel forged under a blue moon, then you m<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    This is the only way you can learn how to read a book:<br />First, you must slay 5 dragons with a sword made from steel forged under a blue moon, then you must grind up the scales of the dragons and mix them with the feathers of a phoenix, the talons of a eagle, and the teeth of a werewolf. Then you must find the entrance to an alternate dimension, go through the wardrobe to Narnia, and climb all the way up Mount Olympus while using a ladder made from solid gold. Speak to the oracle of Delphi and offer your life to the gods. If you followed all of the steps exactly as described, the oracle will reward you with the extremely rare ability to read books. If you missed even one step, the oracle will strike you down.<br />Good luck!<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<div id="review_149465302" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149465302" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149465302?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=mysteries-thrillers-horror">mysteries-thrillers-horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149465302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8688383893555511892">3.5 stars<br/><br/>I only know <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/157676.Lauren_Myracle' title='Lauren Myracle' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lauren Myracle</a>'s name in connection with her <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/301023.ttyl__Internet_Girls___1_' title='ttyl (Internet Girls, #1) by Lauren Myracle' rel='nofollow noopener'>ttyl</a> books. I haven't read that series, but it's pretty safe to say <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8928054.Shine' title='Shine by Lauren Myracle' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shine</a> is nothing like those stories about girls texting each other (or whatever they do). <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8928054.Shine' title='Shine by Lauren Myracle' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shine</a> is most and foremost a story about small-town bigotry. Cat's childhood gay friend Patrick is brutally assaulted - hit with a baseball bat, tied to a gas pump with a fuel nozzle stuffed in his mouth, with words <i>Suck this, faggot</i> written on his bare chest in blood. Small </span>
  <span id="freeText8688383893555511892" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />I only know <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/157676.Lauren_Myracle" title="Lauren Myracle" rel="nofollow noopener">Lauren Myracle</a>'s name in connection with her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/301023.ttyl__Internet_Girls___1_" title="ttyl (Internet Girls, #1) by Lauren Myracle" rel="nofollow noopener">ttyl</a> books. I haven't read that series, but it's pretty safe to say <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8928054.Shine" title="Shine by Lauren Myracle" rel="nofollow noopener">Shine</a> is nothing like those stories about girls texting each other (or whatever they do). <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8928054.Shine" title="Shine by Lauren Myracle" rel="nofollow noopener">Shine</a> is most and foremost a story about small-town bigotry. Cat's childhood gay friend Patrick is brutally assaulted - hit with a baseball bat, tied to a gas pump with a fuel nozzle stuffed in his mouth, with words <i>Suck this, faggot</i> written on his bare chest in blood. Small town of Black Creek, NC, is shaken by this crime, but no one seems to be interested much in solving it. Nobody that is, except Cat. She undertakes this quest because she thinks she owes it to Patrick for her earlier betrayal of him. Cat's amateur investigation not only results in solving the crime, but helps her overcome demons of her own - demons that forced her to end her friendship with Patrick and detach herself from the community years prior.<br /><br />I remember laughing and rolling my eyes at reviews praising <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304335.Beautiful_Creatures__Caster_Chronicles___1_" title="Beautiful Creatures (Caster Chronicles, #1) by Kami Garcia" rel="nofollow noopener">Beautiful Creatures</a>'s portrayal of South. Not so here. Myracle writes Black Creek in a way that I believe - it's beautiful and it's ugly. You have a tightly knit community, but you also have judgment, prejudice, narrow-mindedness, church gossip, sweeping serious stuff under the rug, bowing to the richest, poverty and, of course, meth. Meth is a major player here. Which is probably not such a big surprise. Black Creek <i>is</i> a backward town.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8928054.Shine" title="Shine by Lauren Myracle" rel="nofollow noopener">Shine</a> is full of colorful and colorfully troubled characters. Each comes with a powerful and often heartbreaking story of her/his own. I will remember many of them, but one wackiest kid ever named Robert I will remember best. <br /><br />The mystery of Patrick's assault is one of the strongest I've read in YA fiction. It is sufficiently complex and the investigation itself is not absurd like that one performed by our homegirl Nora in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664.Hush__Hush__Hush__Hush___1_" title="Hush, Hush (Hush, Hush, #1) by Becca Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">Hush, Hush</a>, for instance. The mystery did keep me guessing until the very end, even though I admit, I am a pretty dense mystery solver. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8928054.Shine" title="Shine by Lauren Myracle" rel="nofollow noopener">Shine</a> is not without its laws however. There are some rough spots in the story that could have been done better. For instance, the story line concerning Cat's "incident" that forced her to turn away from her friends, when elaborated on, turns out to be a little convoluted and underwhelming, especially when you read how exactly the event unfolded and how people involved reacted to it. I also thought that the romantic element in the novel was completely tacked on. Not only Cat's meeting with her love interest is too convenient and coincidental to be believed, but this person's presence is the story is unnecessary. I felt like Myracle put it in just to follow some unspoken rules of YA fiction which probably state that there <b>has</b> to be some romance, otherwise a teen book is a no-go.<br /><br />All in all, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8928054.Shine" title="Shine by Lauren Myracle" rel="nofollow noopener">Shine</a> is an emotional, intense, hard-to-put-down story that explores sexuality, violence, addiction and hate in a meaningful way. It is definitely worth checking out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8688383893555511892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_235574551" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235574551" />
    <a title="Nancy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/763271-nancy"><img alt="Nancy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435597527p2/763271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235574551?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy" href="/user/show/763271-nancy">Nancy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=kids-and-teens">kids-and-teens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=outlaw-reviews">outlaw-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=award-winners">award-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/763271-nancy?shelf=shelf-inflicted">shelf-inflicted</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235574551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8792954988829293437"><b>Cross-posted at <a href='http://reviews.logophilos.net/index.php/2012/04/shine-by-lauren-myracle/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Outlaw Reviews</a> and at <a href='http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2014/05/shine.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shelf Inflicted</a> </b><br/><br/>I became curious about this book after it was mistakenly nominated as a finalist for the National Book Awards, instead of another similar-sounding title. It also appealed to me because it is about teenagers growing up in the rural south, the problems kids normally deal with, and the bigotry, poverty, drug addiction, and provincialism that affects everyone.<br/><br/>17-year-old openly gay Patrick lies comatose in a hospital bed after a brutal beating th</span>
  <span id="freeText8792954988829293437" style="display:none"><b>Cross-posted at <a href="http://reviews.logophilos.net/index.php/2012/04/shine-by-lauren-myracle/" rel="nofollow noopener">Outlaw Reviews</a> and at <a href="http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2014/05/shine.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelf Inflicted</a> </b><br /><br />I became curious about this book after it was mistakenly nominated as a finalist for the National Book Awards, instead of another similar-sounding title. It also appealed to me because it is about teenagers growing up in the rural south, the problems kids normally deal with, and the bigotry, poverty, drug addiction, and provincialism that affects everyone.<br /><br />17-year-old openly gay Patrick lies comatose in a hospital bed after a brutal beating that occurred at the convenience store where he works. Though the evidence proves this is a hate crime, the town sheriff is quick to write it off and blame outsiders. Patrick’s friend, Cat, feels the truth is a lot closer to home and sets out to investigate despite admonitions to “leave it be”. <br /><br />Living in a large city comes with its own set of problems, but after reading this story I’m really glad I didn’t grow up in the rural south. I hate the well-meaning, but too inquisitive people, and the fact that anything you do can become the subject of gossip, never to be forgotten. I hate the insular society that does not welcome change or embrace differences, the suspicious people who judge others, yet keep their own shameful secrets well hidden. <br /><br />This is a gripping, realistic story with deeply flawed characters and a vivid setting. Cat’s own past has kept her from fully engaging with the people in her life, but Patrick’s savage attack breaks her out of her shell and forces her to peel back layers of the town’s façade to learn the truth about others and herself. <br /><br />It is a grim story with many wounded souls, many problems, and few solutions. Patrick may be the most obvious victim, but he is far from the only one. And that just makes me sad.<br /><br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_149778012" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149778012" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149778012?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149778012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8821419949720352583">3.5 stars<br/><br/>I'm always a little guilty and anxious when I give books a lower rating than all my friends. I'll be wondering, why didn't I like it, did I miss something there? With Shine, it was double the anxiety, since both Ceilidh and Tatiana loved it, and I respect their opinions quite a bit! But somehow, this book fell short for me, maybe because I expected too much of it. <br/><br/>Shine is about sixteen year old Cat, a girl from a small Southern town whose friend falls victim to a hate crime. When it be</span>
  <span id="freeText8821419949720352583" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />I'm always a little guilty and anxious when I give books a lower rating than all my friends. I'll be wondering, why didn't I like it, did I miss something there? With Shine, it was double the anxiety, since both Ceilidh and Tatiana loved it, and I respect their opinions quite a bit! But somehow, this book fell short for me, maybe because I expected too much of it. <br /><br />Shine is about sixteen year old Cat, a girl from a small Southern town whose friend falls victim to a hate crime. When it becomes obvious that the local authorities are going to do nothing to bring the perpetrators to book, Cat decides to solve the mystery of the gay-basher herself. <br /><br />This book has a lot going for it. I loved how atmospheric the writing was; it pulled me right in, so much so that I could almost envision the darkness of the forest, the squalor of an almost-ghost town, the small town folk rigidly holding on to the remnants of their life. It's a bleak portrayal, but not entirely depressing. <br /><br />Cat is a great character, for the most part. I loved the way she was portrayed, as a flawed, scared girl who slowly emerges from her shell to realize her potential. Her abuse and her subsequent withdrawal from her friends was realistic and heart-breaking. I like the fact that she's not an all-guns-firing crusader who is super-human and impervious to fear and hurt. She is a surprisingly introspective character, and Myracle does a great job in chronicling her growth. <br /><br />I also liked the portrayal of the secondary characters in this book. What I really liked about Shine is that there is no good guy or bad guy. They are all very <i>human</i>, trapped by circumstances and their own desires, with good sides and bad sides to all of their personalities. From Christian, who is still friends with Cat's worst enemy, to her aunt, who likes to ignore reality, to Tommy, who is a Class A jerk, they all have flaws, but Myracle shows us that things are not always what they seem, and sometimes, redemption is possible. <br /><br />There are so many things I liked and admired about this book, that I almost feel bad giving it a 3-star rating. But two things really bugged me about this novel. The first was the pacing. Over half the book passes with next to no plot development. I guess this is part of what contributes to the atmosphere I mentioned before, but I had to positively slog my way through some sections because of the meandering style of Cat's narration. <br /><br />The second was the mystery. It took me about one-tenth the time it did Cat to figure out perpetrator and motive. And I didn't do this because of my awesome telepathic superpowers, or my Holmes-like detective skills, but simply because the answer was so obvious. I don't like mysteries that fizzle out like that. Perhaps the hate crime was only a vehicle for an exposition on life in a small Southern town, but that is still no excuse for not handling it with a little élan. Also, Cat was very slow to arrive at the same conclusion, which annoyed me because I was jumping up and down on my bed screaming, 'Figure it out already, stupid!'<br /><br />I don't have much to say about the romance, since it didn't really play any part in the actual plot. Which is also kind of disappointing, because it felt too convenient. Like Myracle wasn't sure people would read this book if she didn't put at least a little romance in it. But Cat just fell for Jason so quickly and smoothly, with no hitch. Despite being a victim of abuse at an age when it would have scarred her for life. With no therapy and no support, she just got over it and decided to kiss a boy she's known two weeks? <br /><br />I DID like this book, but not as much as I thought I would. It's more of a descriptive novel, that kind that pulls you in at the moment, rather than one that leaves a lasting impression. My recommendation? Read it. <br /><br />P.S. An ARC of this book was provided to me by the publishers via Net Galley. No external considerations affected this review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8821419949720352583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_151965150" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151965150" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151965150?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=bad-shit-and-atrocities">bad-shit-and-atrocities</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=highly-recommended">highly-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=romance-y">romance-y</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=tear-jerkers">tear-jerkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=religion-y">religion-y</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151965150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6284506243593213788">I've never read any of Lauren Myracle's other books. I'm not much into the whole "txt-spk" thing, so those books have never sparked my interest. Not my cup of tea. Other than those, I couldn't have named another book Myracle had written before today. But this... this book called out to me. Not only because of the absolutely gorgeous cover, but because of the premise, and because it's set in the South. I love me some books set in the South. And because it has Issues. Issues with a capital 'I'.<br/><br/>And</span>
  <span id="freeText6284506243593213788" style="display:none">I've never read any of Lauren Myracle's other books. I'm not much into the whole "txt-spk" thing, so those books have never sparked my interest. Not my cup of tea. Other than those, I couldn't have named another book Myracle had written before today. But this... this book called out to me. Not only because of the absolutely gorgeous cover, but because of the premise, and because it's set in the South. I love me some books set in the South. And because it has Issues. Issues with a capital 'I'.<br /><br />And boy, did this deliver. If it hadn't been written with such grace and honesty, and a light touch and sense of innocence, it could have gone so very, very badly wrong. The Issues in this book are the kind that outsiders abhor and denounce, while those living in and around and with them are almost oblivious to their existence as an 'Issue' at all. To those people, it's just life. Normal. Everyday. This book touched on a lot of things. Poverty, addiction, class division, alcoholism, abuse, homosexuality and homophobia, fear and hatred, small-town politics, friendship and loyalty, etc. So many things that some could have easily gotten lost and confused. But even with all of these issues entwined throughout the story, I never felt that it forgot what it was.<br /><br />I loved the way this story was written. I love the way it was parceled out, little by little, edging closer to the truth and the consequences and the brokenness, like a hungry mouse sneaking closer to a crumb not far from the cat's bed. The mouse knows that rushing will cause it to lose its chance, to be hurt -- but caution and stealth may win it a chance to survive. This book was like that. It crept along, building momentum, until it reached where it needed to be. <br /><br />I instantly fell in love with these characters, especially Cat and Patrick. My heart broke for the things that they lost, both before and after Patrick is beaten and left for dead. I loved their friendship, and the simple acceptance of it. I loved Mama Sweetie, Patrick's Grandma, and her kindness and wisdom and faith. I usually find it hard to accept religion in books, because so very often it comes across as preachy. That was not the case here. It was less religion and more a matter of faith - a simple knowledge that there's something and someone there for us. No judgment, no fire and brimstone, no recriminations for every little thought, just a sense of "If you want, you can - if not, that's OK too." I liked that. <br /><br />This book is gorgeous and amazing from cover to cover, and I was so wrapped up in this community and these lives that I almost didn't want to see, but I couldn't look away. I found one thing, one little thing, about the very end to be a bit unbelievable, but I understand it, and I wasn't disappointed. All in all, I loved this book and I think it's one that I will need to own, to re-read and absorb and love. <br /><br />It's that good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6284506243593213788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_683238189" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/683238189" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4844873-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299680097p2/4844873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/683238189?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/4844873-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer683238189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8194411490137557673"><br/><b>”…you can cast off the darkness and shine again, can’t you?”</b><br/><br/>Shine tells the story of a brutal crime in a small town. Patrick Truman is found beaten and left for dead. Cat, Patrick’s best friend, is determined to find out what happened no matter what. Readers jump, right along with Cat, into the storm of small town gossip, fear, and hatred to find the truth.<br/><br/>First and foremost—I have to gush about the writing. Language, words, and descriptions that pulled me in at page one. I was there. On the mou</span>
  <span id="freeText8194411490137557673" style="display:none"><br /><b>”…you can cast off the darkness and shine again, can’t you?”</b><br /><br />Shine tells the story of a brutal crime in a small town. Patrick Truman is found beaten and left for dead. Cat, Patrick’s best friend, is determined to find out what happened no matter what. Readers jump, right along with Cat, into the storm of small town gossip, fear, and hatred to find the truth.<br /><br />First and foremost—I have to gush about the writing. Language, words, and descriptions that pulled me in at page one. I was there. On the mountain. In the room. In the gossip. I could feel it all—”heavy foliage dappling the road with green shadows and pockets of shade”. You will feel this world on your skin. And the sayings…haha…oh, how I loved the down-home talk that made the town and characters so unique and in a land of their own. Lines that made me stop, tilt my head, and say “Huh?”---“The sun don’t shine on the same dog’s tail all the time.” Ms. Myracle has a very powerful way with words that held me close. Pulled me in. That said though, it was the characters that will live in my heart. Strong, memorable, flawed, heart breaking characters that had me giggling, sighing, and cheering.<br /><br />The relationship that left the deepest dent in my heart and soul was between Cat and her brother, Christian. One hell of a heart wrenching pull, power, and connection. I found tears in my eyes more than once when those two tried to talk or just be. One of the worst feelings in the world is when we feel let down or betrayed by family. No one but family can tear us up in such a devastating and complete way. Broke my heart.<br /><br />Cat. Cat. Cat. I tend to be hard on my female characters. But damn! Girl, you made me proud! Throughout the book, the importance of speaking the truth, letting it out, not hiding is woven through the pages and mystery. Cat was hell bent on finding out what happened to Patrick. But to do that, she had to find and speak up for herself as well. She had to stand up to her own demons, pain, and past. And I loved her for it! She did it with sass, smarts, and strength.<br /> <br /><b>“I didn’t hide or run away or pretend the ugliness didn’t happen. I stood up and said something that was true. I said it out loud, and by doing so, I was standing up for lots of people, not just me.”</b><br /><br />But that same point and love also plays into the main reason why the ending disappointed me. I’m talking the last 2 pages. We spent the entire book watching Cat search and uncover the truth in her heart and town. But after everything—what does she do? Warning: BIG spoiler ahead. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Cat suggested/asked Patrick to keep the truth under wraps. My heart’s first instinct was to break and utter—No, no, no wait a minute! Didn’t Cat learn her lesson? Over and over we saw her learn—“hiding had the power to hurt, too”. I understand and realize the truth did come out to some people. But….it still felt wrong. It felt like they were covering up a hurt and truth again.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Still loved the book and ending. That was just one emotion layered in between all the love. Shine is an important, sad, powerful story about acceptance, love, truth, and forgiveness. <br /> <br />Have you ever read a scene or moment in a book and just knew it would stick with you? A moment forever etched in your book memories? Lauren Myracle creates so many of those moments for me here. I will remember every plunge into the water, wind chime twinkle, and “Wanna rub my head?” offer. The raves, gossip, and whispers about Shine have been running through my GR feed and world for a long time. A book with a lot of love surrounding it. I am so happy I finally picked it up.<br /><br />Go read it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8194411490137557673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_203299331" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203299331" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203299331?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203299331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4281027644912414667">Guys, I survived reading my first young-adult book as an adult! No English teachers or professors pelted me with stones and no one called me out in the middle of the street! Whew.<br/><br/>Anyway, <i>Shine</i> details the story of sixteen-year-old Cat and the hate crime against her former best friend Patrick. Cat stopped talking to Patrick - along with everyone else at her high school - after an incident involving another boy two years ago. But when Patrick is found brutally beaten to the point of comatose and t</span>
  <span id="freeText4281027644912414667" style="display:none">Guys, I survived reading my first young-adult book as an adult! No English teachers or professors pelted me with stones and no one called me out in the middle of the street! Whew.<br /><br />Anyway, <i>Shine</i> details the story of sixteen-year-old Cat and the hate crime against her former best friend Patrick. Cat stopped talking to Patrick - along with everyone else at her high school - after an incident involving another boy two years ago. But when Patrick is found brutally beaten to the point of comatose and the police blame it on out-of-town college students, Cat sets out to uncover the truth. On her journey she confronts small town gossip, dangerous drugs, a college boy named Jason, and a startling discovery concerning Patrick's near-fatal encounter.<br /><br />Lauren Myracle writes a mystery with <i>Shine</i>. While many other factors may stick out - the southern setting, meth, hate crimes against gays, etc. - all of these are supplementary to the center storyline of the novel. Cat's mission involves finding the truth about what happened to Patrick and more or less doling out justice; Myracle accomplishes this plot with no hiccups or awkwardness.<br /><br />Perhaps a few more themes could have been expanded to provide more pathos, but as far as mystery goes Myracle's <i>Shine</i> sticks out as one of the best in the YA genre I've read. She includes a likeable yet still-growing protagonist, a solid cast of characters with only a few archetypes, and an omnipresent sense of place. Recommended for those who want a quick mystery read and for fans of Myracle's other works.<br /><br />*review cross-posted on my blog, <a href="http://thequietvoice18.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">the quiet voice</a>.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_259744155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/259744155" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7389327-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441123090p2/7389327.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/259744155?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/7389327-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer259744155&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer259744155" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5215572703718433246">I'm surprised by all the attention the book received. For me it just didn't work. I was expecting a story about homophobia, but it doesn't really explore that theme. It's really about Cat, her issues, and finding her courage to stand up for what is right. I can get on board with that. Justice! Still, I was disappointed at every turn. Stereotypes abound so much that I can't think of a single character that had any depth. Not to mention that most characters were unlikable, including Cat. I also ha</span>
  <span id="freeText5215572703718433246" style="display:none">I'm surprised by all the attention the book received. For me it just didn't work. I was expecting a story about homophobia, but it doesn't really explore that theme. It's really about Cat, her issues, and finding her courage to stand up for what is right. I can get on board with that. Justice! Still, I was disappointed at every turn. Stereotypes abound so much that I can't think of a single character that had any depth. Not to mention that most characters were unlikable, including Cat. I also had trouble with unbelievable plot elements like the fact that Cat didn't speak to her friends for 3 years after her trauma. Three years?! How? Would she have lived to be a bitter old hermit lady if Patrick wasn't attacked and nearly killed?<br /><br />Even the ending was a massive disappointment. Cat decides not to tell anyone who Patrick's attacker was. Maybe she thought justice had been served but keeping silent won't help change the community. Maybe she feels that the town is doomed to be consumed by meth anyway. Cat also decides not to tell anyone about the boy who raped her because he apologized. WHAT?! He traumatized her so badly that her life fell apart for YEARS but it's okay now because he said he's sorry? Myracle brought up some important issues and themes but fails to develop or resolve them in any satisfying way.<br /><br />-NetGalley advance copy</span>

<div id="review_152378098" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152378098" />
    <a title="Trudi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1416912-trudi"><img alt="Trudi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446613110p2/1416912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152378098?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trudi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trudi" href="/user/show/1416912-trudi">Trudi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781419701849" href="/book/show/12821061-shine">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=a-sense-of-place">a-sense-of-place</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=glbt">glbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=modern-lit">modern-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=the-wonder-years">the-wonder-years</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=twss">twss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=secrets">secrets</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152378098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer851817757770821083">The first time I heard about this book was when the author <a href='http://www.nytimes.com/2011/10/18/books/lauren-myracle-withdraws-shine-from-national-book-awards.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>was pressured to withdraw its National Book Award nomination</a> which had been given in error and intended for the book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8299165.Chime' title='Chime by Franny Billingsley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chime</a>. What rhymes with Shine? Chime apparently. Good grief. Really people, you can't be any more professional than that? <a href='http://www.huffingtonpost.com/lauren-myracle/lauren-myracle-national-book-awards_b_1019972.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The author talks about</a> the emotional whirlwind that followed, but there was a silver lining to the crushing disappointment -- the controversy brought much needed awareness to this quiet, unassuming book</span>
  <span id="freeText851817757770821083" style="display:none">The first time I heard about this book was when the author <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2011/10/18/books/lauren-myracle-withdraws-shine-from-national-book-awards.html" rel="nofollow noopener">was pressured to withdraw its National Book Award nomination</a> which had been given in error and intended for the book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8299165.Chime" title="Chime by Franny Billingsley" rel="nofollow noopener">Chime</a>. What rhymes with Shine? Chime apparently. Good grief. Really people, you can't be any more professional than that? <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/lauren-myracle/lauren-myracle-national-book-awards_b_1019972.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The author talks about</a> the emotional whirlwind that followed, but there was a silver lining to the crushing disappointment -- the controversy brought much needed awareness to this quiet, unassuming book. <br /><br /><i>Shine</i> isn't a dystopia. It has no post-apocalyptic cachet, there are no demons, angels, vampires or fairies. Instead, <i>Shine</i> is a lyrical and realistic coming-of-age portrait of a young girl living in a small backwoods Southern town. Cat is 16 and knows all about secrets. She has been carrying a dark and bitter one of her own for three years. It has caused her to wither and withdraw, and worst of all it has cost her Patrick. <br /><br />Patrick is Cat's best friend but she hasn't spoken to him, not really, since "the bad thing". Patrick is set adrift without her and finds the only friends left to him are members of "the redneck posse" who tease and berate him mercilessly for being gay. One night Patrick is brutally beaten and left for dead outside of the gas station where he works. The nature of the assault has labeled this a hate crime and Cat -- fueled by guilt and anger -- becomes desperate to find out who has done this to her gentle friend. She believes it's someone she knows, and the closer she gets to unraveling the truth, the more dangerous it becomes for everyone around her, including Patrick who lies helpless in a coma. <br /><br />In many ways, this has all the hallmarks of a good mystery. I love how Becky describes it in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151965150" rel="nofollow noopener">her review</a> as: <blockquote>parceled out, little by little, edging closer to the truth and the consequences and the brokenness, like a hungry mouse sneaking closer to a crumb not far from the cat's bed. The mouse knows that rushing will cause it to lose its chance, to be hurt -- but caution and stealth may win it a chance to survive. This book was like that. It crept along, building momentum, until it reached where it needed to be. </blockquote> <i>Shine</i> isn't a gentle story -- it is a raw and honest consideration of self-acceptance, self-loathing, guilt, friendship and family. There is explicit language and vivid descriptions of violence. Despite the ugliness there is much beauty to consider as well, and Myracle's prose reminded me both of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112525.Winter_s_Bone" title="Winter's Bone by Daniel Woodrell" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter's Bone</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2657.To_Kill_a_Mockingbird" title="To Kill a Mockingbird by Harper Lee" rel="nofollow noopener">To Kill a Mockingbird</a>. <br /><br />This book has its flaws, but overall it accomplishes something wonderful. </span>
  <a data-text-id="851817757770821083" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3298750999881067519">Set in a small town in the South, this book is about bigotry, and friendship, and love. It's about seeing the best in people, and seeing the worst. It is a beautifully written story about a brutal hate crime. <br/><br/>Cat's best friend, Patrick, is the victim of a gay bashing--smashed in the head with a bat, tied to a gas pump with the nozzle shoved in his mouth, and the words <i>Suck this faggot</i> written on his chest in blood. He is in a coma, and they don't know if he's going to make it. <br/><br/>The small town cop</span>
  <span id="freeText3298750999881067519" style="display:none">Set in a small town in the South, this book is about bigotry, and friendship, and love. It's about seeing the best in people, and seeing the worst. It is a beautifully written story about a brutal hate crime. <br /><br />Cat's best friend, Patrick, is the victim of a gay bashing--smashed in the head with a bat, tied to a gas pump with the nozzle shoved in his mouth, and the words <i>Suck this faggot</i> written on his chest in blood. He is in a coma, and they don't know if he's going to make it. <br /><br />The small town cops would rather not look too closely at the crime, they would prefer to act as if they are investigating, and then just blame it on some punks passing through town, and sweep the whole big mess under the rug. Because really, it could have been anyone--small town homophobia runs deep.<br /><br />But Cat wants to find out who hurt Patrick, so she starts investigating on her own. Which is easier said than done, especially since she's shut out everyone in her life after something happened to her, something that no one knows about, even the reader. She's shut out everyone, including Patrick, including her brother, Christian. So getting people to open up to her proves to be more difficult that she had hoped.<br /><br />There were a few things I wasn't crazy about--particularly Cat's love interest, whose name I don't even remember 3 days later. He was totally one dimensional and so completely unneeded to the story. He could have been edited out and the book would have been better for it. Also, the big reveal of Cat's traumatic "secret" ended up being a bit underwhelming, and it's resolution felt altogether too nice and tidy for my liking.<br /><br />But other than that, this was a beautiful book. The mystery was done nicely, with enough suspense to last until the whodunnit reveal. I popped around through the entire book, <i>"It was him. No, it was him. Hmmm...maybe it was him?"</i> and still I was pretty shocked when the truth came out.<br /><br />Lauren Myracle tackled a bunch of tough issues in this book--abuse, alcoholism, homosexuality, homophobia, drug use, small town politics, class warfare, small mindedness &amp; ignorance--and she did it beautifully.<br /><br /><br /><i>*I received this as a free ARC from NetGalley, in exchange for my review. No goodies (other than the story) were acquired by me.*</i></span>

<div id="review_140346157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140346157" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4176166-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600307841p2/4176166.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140346157?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/4176166-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=atlp-review">atlp-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140346157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14942571250485432736"><b>This review may also be found on <a><i>A Thousand Little Pages</i></a>.</b><br/><br/>An <a>article</a> recently came out in the Wall Street Journal that generated quite a buzz in the young adult book community. It basically slanders every YA novel out there that is “dark” by their standards and indirectly blames the books for familiarizing and possibly prompting trauma, violence, and profanity within the average teen. <i>Shine</i> received an honorary place in the article and was complained about quite a bit. So, dear Ms. Gurdon, author</span>
  <span id="freeText14942571250485432736" style="display:none"><b>This review may also be found on <a><i>A Thousand Little Pages</i></a>.</b><br /><br />An <a>article</a> recently came out in the Wall Street Journal that generated quite a buzz in the young adult book community. It basically slanders every YA novel out there that is “dark” by their standards and indirectly blames the books for familiarizing and possibly prompting trauma, violence, and profanity within the average teen. <i>Shine</i> received an honorary place in the article and was complained about quite a bit. So, dear Ms. Gurdon, author of said article, I am a teenager. I have read <i>Shine</i>, among tons of other “dark” novels. Do I now feel the inclination to begin stimulating the nearest meth business or sexually assaulting my classmates? No. No, I don’t. Not at all.<br /><br />Since I’ve read Ms. Myracle’s <i>Internet Girls</i> series prior to <i>Shine</i>, I simply dismissed her as a frivolous author. Well, all my expectations disappeared down the drain as I read the first page, which featured a newspaper clipping detailing the attack of a gay teen in the tiny town of Black Creek. The novel goes on to describe the protagonist’s search for the truth about what really happened to the teen, an old childhood friend named Patrick.<br /><br />Ms. Myracle’s writing created a sort of thick and somber atmosphere throughout the book, which was appropriate given the gravity of the topic. Her characters are easy to sympathize for, and the mystery involved was not overly obvious or completely impossible to solve. A multitude of touchy subjects were tackled and handled delicately. Overall, I enjoyed <i>Shine</i> a lot more than I’d originally thought I would.<br /><br />Even with all the hate and despair in the story, I finished the novel with a feeling of hope. Yes, WSJ article, maybe it wasn’t a happily ever after, maybe the characters experienced things no one should go through. But there is hope and healing everywhere if you look hard enough.<br /><br />Book Source: ARC from Abrams Books via NetGalley</span>
  <a data-text-id="14942571250485432736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_157542962" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157542962" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/867629-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404333616p2/867629.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157542962?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/867629-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867629-justin?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867629-justin?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867629-justin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867629-justin?shelf=shelf-of-fame">shelf-of-fame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/867629-justin?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157542962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16245584190985786403">This is the first of Myracle’s books that I’ve read, since her popular Internet Girls series is well outside the realm of my interest. However, after reading Shine, I may have to take a look at those books after all. I managed to secure an advance reader’s copy after hearing some other librarians rave about this book, and while initially skeptical, I was surprised at how quickly this book grabbed me. While it has its oddities and weak spots, Shine is a powerful, well-written book that does an ex</span>
  <span id="freeText16245584190985786403" style="display:none">This is the first of Myracle’s books that I’ve read, since her popular Internet Girls series is well outside the realm of my interest. However, after reading Shine, I may have to take a look at those books after all. I managed to secure an advance reader’s copy after hearing some other librarians rave about this book, and while initially skeptical, I was surprised at how quickly this book grabbed me. While it has its oddities and weak spots, Shine is a powerful, well-written book that does an excellent job of framing gritty, tough themes for a teen audience.<br /><br />The story opens with a newspaper story out of a rural North Carolina town called Black Creek. A teenager named Patrick is known to all the residents of the backwoods town as both the amiable clerk at the local gas station and the village oddity for being openly gay. When Patrick is found severely beaten and tied to a gas pump with a homophobic slur scrawled on his chest, the town is awash with horrified, and almost gleeful, gossip. Cat, a withdrawn sixteen-year-old girl, is particular affected; Patrick was once her closest friend, though she had not been speaking with him at the time of his assault. In a small town where everyone knows everyone, Cat is convinced that she can succeed where the local sheriff is failing, and discover the truth behind what happened to Patrick. Her guilt over the way in which she had handled their friendship drives her to find Patrick’s attacker amidst the residents of Black Creek, and repeated advice from those around her to let sleeping dogs lie only stokes the flames of her anger. However, her quest to shine light on the crime raises the frightening possibility of her being the next target. <br /><br />This is a rough story to read. It starts with a gut punch and doesn’t get much better. Homophobia, meth addiction, and sexual assault are all touched upon in this story. For all of its darkness, though, Shine never really dips into sensationalism or angst. Everything seems very real in this book. Black Creek is a rural town with rural problems and rural attitudes; while I didn’t grow up as poor as Cat did, I do have enough experience with small-town mindsets to have the setting and characters resonate in a very real way with me. And for all of the darkness in Black Creek, there is beauty, too. Myracle is obviously writing what she knows, and has a talent for presenting the South in a sublime, evocative way, warts and all.<br /><br />I figured out the mystery early on, but that’s only because I’m fairly familiar with how stories like these play out, unfortunately. But the main plot was extremely well done, with enough tension to keep astute readers strung along but without being too obtuse or boring for teens. The characters are layered, and many are both sympathetic and menacing by turns. Cat, the narrator, is particularly well-written, and her story is visceral and heartbreaking. While the plot itself is something that we have seen before, the mystery in Shine is made compelling by how ambiguous it is, and how there are things left mysterious and unexplained even as the story takes familiar turns.<br /><br />There are a few things that bothered me, at least momentarily. The introduction of Cat’s love interest (and another potential suspect) is so abrupt that at first I wondered what their first scene together was even doing in the book. The explanation of the tension between Cat and her brother near the end of the book is also somewhat confounding, and appears almost contrived at first glance. The ending, too, is somewhat of a letdown. This could be because I figured the mystery out early on and was hoping I was wrong (I was almost completely correct), but the book also ends abruptly and on a strangely positive note, considering how horrible Patrick’s ordeal was and how bleak things still are by the end of the story.<br /><br />All of these problems spring from a single source, though, and that source is actually the book's biggest strength: the characters in Shine are not stereotypes, despite their corn-fed hillbilly slang, and they do not act in a predictable fashion. There are no easy answers, here, just as there aren’t any in real life. Sometimes relationships do start in strange, abrupt ways, and considering that Shine is a book for teens, it follows the romance formula in way that is refreshingly understated. While the actions of Cat’s brother in the face of her earliest childhood trauma initially ring false to me and, I imagine, every other big brother who reads this book, Christian’s odd reaction is still evocatively real, in that it proves that not everyone is as brave as they seem. And while the mystery played itself out in the way it was foreshadowed (brilliantly, I might add), I am convinced that another character was involved. I am absolutely sure of this, due to multiple hints in the writing, and despite the fact that the ending does not make any mention of it and wraps things up with a single climactic confrontation. Whether this is an intentional tease by Myracle or just my own interpretation of the reading, it’s still a byproduct of a gripping, tightly-plotted mystery, and lends credence to Black Creek’s gritty, bittersweet realism.<br /><br />For all that I looked for things to criticize, Shine wouldn’t let me go. I tore through the book, and loved every part of it. This is a grim, unflinching take on the consequences of secrecy and self-loathing, and it also is a paean to the lonely beauty and restorative power of a small, tightly-knit community. It offers a hard glimpse into reality while still telling an oddly sweet story, and it provides a moral without preaching. While there are occasions that the themes could be explored a little deeper or with more detail, this is a perfect example of dramatic teen lit. Once it hit shelves, I imagine it will move quickly. I’d recommend this to anyone looking for a good mystery, regardless of age.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16245584190985786403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_163712601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163712601" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1313520-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257953885p2/1313520.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163712601?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/1313520-julia">Julia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1313520-julia?shelf=friendship-school">friendship-school</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer163712601&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163712601" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11013387105473316042">I didn't love this book. It contained one of my pet peeves. I'll get there in a minute.<br/><br/>The mystery element is adequate, despite one character that feels forced & the telegraphing for the last 3/4 of the book of the major clue revealed at the climax. I'm not a fan of mysteries as a genre, partially because I usually see the answer coming & rarely find them compelling. It takes a great one to hold me & this wasn't that book for me. That's just a matter of personal taste, mind. A mystery fan might </span>
  <span id="freeText11013387105473316042" style="display:none">I didn't love this book. It contained one of my pet peeves. I'll get there in a minute.<br /><br />The mystery element is adequate, despite one character that feels forced &amp; the telegraphing for the last 3/4 of the book of the major clue revealed at the climax. I'm not a fan of mysteries as a genre, partially because I usually see the answer coming &amp; rarely find them compelling. It takes a great one to hold me &amp; this wasn't that book for me. That's just a matter of personal taste, mind. A mystery fan might just enjoy this book &amp; think it was a great story.<br /><br />However, I simply can't get past another story where the main character was sexually assaulted &amp; and an adult knew about it, but did nothing. There is not one responsible or useful adult in this book. The father is a drunk &amp; the aunt blinds herself. When the aunt actually witnesses the assault, she pretends nothing happened, or maybe that it was consentual? The aunt's denial is so blatant that it is not only painful but unrealisticly unbelievable in this day &amp; age. Regardless, the girl was 13 &amp; attacked by a 16 year old boy. YOU STOP THAT NO MATTER WHETHER OR NOT YOU THINK IT IS CONSENTUAL BECAUSE IT IS NOT NEVER &amp; IN NO WAY OKAY!!!<br /><br />To use an incident like the above as a plot device for your main character - who has isolated herself for 3 years, but now is reaching out to solve the mystery of her gay friend's attack - just seems cheap. If you needed a character to grow out of isolation ther are other ways to do it. If you need adults out of the way, there are other ways to do that too. I am just sick of stories that reinforce the idea that young adults can't actually go to adults in times of crisis because they won't be helped. That's what I felt this story did. I can't get past my irritation on this issue to actually enjoy the book. Sorry.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_227859807" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227859807" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2977327-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321148527p2/2977327.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227859807?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/2977327-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227859807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15366067195000907830">I took this book out of the library in righteous indignation, shortly after the NBA debacle. I was poised to love it and hoped that I would, if only to add to my fury. However, I never warmed up to Cat, the main character, which is a huge problem for me. I also didn't like most of the other characters, except for Patrick, who was in a coma and we learned about mostly through flashbacks and dialogue. Cat spent much of the book dwelling on an incident from the past, and once the incident was final</span>
  <span id="freeText15366067195000907830" style="display:none">I took this book out of the library in righteous indignation, shortly after the NBA debacle. I was poised to love it and hoped that I would, if only to add to my fury. However, I never warmed up to Cat, the main character, which is a huge problem for me. I also didn't like most of the other characters, except for Patrick, who was in a coma and we learned about mostly through flashbacks and dialogue. Cat spent much of the book dwelling on an incident from the past, and once the incident was finally revealed in its entirety, it did not seem appalling enough to warrant her complete withdrawal from her former friends (including Patrick) for three years. It bothered me that the coma-inducing incident underlying this book was sort of the impetus for getting Cat to "snap out of it." Also, this technique has been done frequently in YA--where the main character has a secret from the past, either rape or molestation or other mistreatment by the opposite sex--and for it to work and feel original, there has to be something unique about it and there has to be something warranting the character's specific reaction. The incident simply did not warrant three full years of introverted behavior. I was also troubled by the romance that was thrown into this book. Although it was basically just a flirtation that we knew would lead to more after the events of the book, it seemed out of place and thrown in because YA supposedly always needs a hint of romance. I also never liked Jason, because I couldn't forgive him for the horrible name he called Cat at the library, even if she could forgive him. Just not an endearing introduction to the love interest, if there really had to be one in this book. I felt the climax was somewhat ridiculous as it unfolded, and I had too many moments of needing to suspend disbelief. I was quite perturbed by the number of typographical errors in this book as well. I reluctantly gave it two stars; it is slightly above a one for me, if only because it is clear that the author does have solid writing skills and a gift for imagery. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15366067195000907830" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_236401977" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236401977" />
    <a title="Halley Todd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6345187-halley-todd"><img alt="Halley Todd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458157563p2/6345187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236401977?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Halley Todd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Halley Todd" href="/user/show/6345187-halley-todd">Halley Todd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6345187-halley-todd?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6345187-halley-todd?shelf=si-624-reviews">si-624-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6345187-halley-todd?shelf=family-love">family-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6345187-halley-todd?shelf=boys">boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6345187-halley-todd?shelf=mature">mature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6345187-halley-todd?shelf=drugs">drugs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6345187-halley-todd?shelf=sexual-abuse">sexual-abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6345187-halley-todd?shelf=overcoming-obstacles">overcoming-obstacles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6345187-halley-todd?shelf=homosexuality">homosexuality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6345187-halley-todd?shelf=banned-books">banned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236401977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2664016039371150190">This poignant tale about a supposed hate crime in a small North Carolinian town is not for faint-hearted readers. 16-year old Cat must finally come out of her self-imposed exile from her community when her childhood best friend is put into a coma. Patrick was found outside the convenience store where he worked. He was hit in the head with a baseball bat, a gas nozzle was shoved down his throat, and scrawled across his chest in blood were the words: “Suck on this f-----.” The town is eager to bla</span>
  <span id="freeText2664016039371150190" style="display:none">This poignant tale about a supposed hate crime in a small North Carolinian town is not for faint-hearted readers. 16-year old Cat must finally come out of her self-imposed exile from her community when her childhood best friend is put into a coma. Patrick was found outside the convenience store where he worked. He was hit in the head with a baseball bat, a gas nozzle was shoved down his throat, and scrawled across his chest in blood were the words: “Suck on this f-----.” The town is eager to blame drunk out of towners. However, Cat suspects otherwise. As she digs deeper into this mystery, she realizes how much things in her community had stayed the same, but also how much people she had known her whole life had changed, including her. There are people that don’t want her to learn the truth, but she is determined the right the wrongs done to her, and to fix the wrongs she has done.<br /><br />What impresses me the most about this novel is the author’s voice. Myracle has done a fabulous job of fleshing out each character, whether minor or major. Every character is dynamic in some way, and all feel distinctly human in their flaws, but also in their good attributes. The reader is reminded that every person has good and bad, and that not every bad person started out that way. I find it amazing that this novel is able to end on such a hopeful note despite all of the rottenness that exists in Cat and Patrick’s community. Once a reader begins the investigation with Cat, they will be unable to put this novel down until the wrongs are righted, and justice is served. While this novel is highly recommended for extremely, and I do stress the extremely, mature readers in grades 10-12, I would suggest that an adult discuss issues presented with a young reader. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2664016039371150190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
